The Syllogism
advanced
10 min
Understanding Qiyas al-Musawat and the Classification of Syllogisms
Defense of qiyas al-musawat as part of muwasil bi al-dhat and categorical syllogism despite lack of repeated middle term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the dialectical exchange around qiyas al-musawat, identify the distinction between conditions for production and conditions for knowledge, and evaluate the validity of the syllogism.

Core Idea
Qiyas al-Musawat is valid even without a repeated middle term; repetition is for knowledge, not production.

In this passage, the commentator defends qiyas al-musawat (equality syllogism) as part of the essential productive syllogisms (muwasil bi al-dhat). An objector argues it cannot fit the four figures due to lacking a shared middle term. The resolution introduces a key distinction between conditions for actual production and conditions for our knowledge of that production, preserving the syllogism's validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial problem
The objector points out that qiyas al-musawat cannot be placed in any of the four figures of the conjunctive categorical syllogism because its premises do not share a middle term in the technical sense (i.e., the middle term is not repeated in the standard way that defines the figures).
2
Recognize the consequence
If the syllogism does not fit any figure, it seems to fall outside the universal definition of categorical syllogism, yet it is still considered a syllogism—leading to a contradiction that would restrict the universal to some individuals.
3
Understand the commentator's response
The commentator distinguishes two types of conditions: (a) conditions for the actual occurrence of the conclusion (intaj) and (b) conditions for our knowledge of the conclusion. The repetition of the middle term is of the second type—it is needed for epistemic certainty, not for the conclusion to follow logically.
4
Apply the distinction to qiyas al-musawat
In qiyas al-musawat, the conclusion does follow from the premises (production occurs), even if we cannot immediately see the logical connection without the repetition. Thus, the syllogism is valid and falls under the categorical syllogism, but not under the figures that require the epistemic condition.
5
Evaluate the commentator's critical note
The commentator adds that even the epistemic condition might be satisfied without repetition in some cases, leaving the issue open for further reflection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و بدونها ليس من اقسام الموصل بالذات : فان : قلت قد سبق آنفاً ان قياس المساواة ينتج بالذات الف مساء المساوى ج مثلاً فكيف يصح الحكم بانه ليس من اقسام الموصل بالذات؟ قلت: هذا بالنسبة الى النتيجة المذكورة سابقاً اعنى قولنا الف مساو لـ «ج» مثلاً لا مطلقا لظهور استلزامه لذلك بلا واسطة كما سبق فهو بالنسبة الى ذلك من اقسام الموصل بالذات و تعريف القياس ايضاً شامل عليه على ما يشهد به التأمل الصادق و ان لم يكن بالنسبة إلى النتيجة المذكورة من فان قلت: لوكان الامر كذلك لزم قصر الكلى على بعض افراده و هو باطل جزماً. اقسامه بيان الملازمة انهم حصروا القياس في الاستثنائى والاقتراني و الاقتراني على الحملى والشرطي و معلوم انه اى القياس المساواة ليس من الاستثنائى ولا الاقتراني الشرطى بقى الاقتراني الحملى وحصروه فى الاشكال الاربعة و ليس بداخل تحت شيء منها للزوم اشتراك المقدمتين في الحد الاوسط بالمعنى الاصطلاحي فيها دونه فثبت انه غير داخل تحت شيء من الاقسام المذكورة للقياس مع انه من افراده كما هو المفروض و هو المطلوب. واما بطلان التالي فظاهر لا يحتاج إلى البيان. قلت: لا شك فى ان قياس المساواة بالنسبة الى ما ذكرنا داخل تحت الاقتراني الحملى على ما يشهد به تعريفه بانه ما كان القول الاخر فيه مذكوراً بمادته دون هيئته ويكون كلتا مقدمتيه حملية. و اما ما ذكر من انهم حصروه فى الاشكال الاربعة و هو ليس بداخل تحت واحد منها لاشتراطهم فيها اشتراك المقدمتين في الحد الاوسط ولا اشتراك فيه هنا فجوابه على ما أشار اليه بعض المحققين انهم لم يشترطوا تكرر الوسط بمعنى انه لولاه لم يتحقق الانتاج بل بمعنى انه لولاه لم يلزم العلم بالانتاج. والحاصل: ان الشروط المعتبرة في الاقيسة الاقترانية على نوعين ماهو شرط لتحقق الانتاج وماهو شرط للعلم به و تكرر الوسط من النوع الثاني وحصرهم القياس الاقتراني في الاشكال الاربعة بالنسبة الى القياس المشتمل على الشروط المعتبرة للعلم بالانتاج لا مطلقا حتى يلزم قصر الكلى على بعض الافراد. ولا يخفى ما فيه، فانا لا تسلم انه لا يلزم العلم بالانتاج اذا لم يتكرر الوسط بالمعنى الاصطلاحي بل اذا لم يتكرر مطلقا ضرورة حصول العلم بالانتاج فى قياس المساواة بالنسبة إلى النتيجة المفروضة مع انه لم يتكرر الأوسط فيه ة بالمعنى المشهور عند الجمهور فتأمل (میرزا محمد علی).
His saying: 'And without it, it is not from the divisions of muwasil bi al-dhat': So if you say: It has already passed that the equality syllogism essentially produces 'A is equal to the equal of C', for example, so how is the judgment correct that it is not from the divisions of muwasil bi al-dhat? I say: This is regarding the result mentioned earlier, namely our statement 'A is equal to C', not absolutely, because its entailment of that without mediation is apparent as before. So regarding that, it is from the divisions of muwasil bi al-dhat, and the definition of syllogism also includes it, as honest reflection testifies. However, if you say: If it were so, then it would necessitate restricting the universal to some of its individuals, which is definitely false. [You mention] its divisions? The explanation of the implication: They have confined the syllogism to the exceptive and the conjunctive, and the conjunctive to the categorical and the conditional. It is known that the equality syllogism is not among the exceptive nor the conjunctive conditional; the categorical remains. And they have confined it to the four figures, and it does not fall under any of them because the two premises must share a middle term in the technical sense in them, while it lacks that. So it is established that it is not included in any of the mentioned divisions of the syllogism, even though it is one of its individuals as assumed, and that is what is required. And the falsity of the consequent is obvious, needing no explanation. I say: There is no doubt that the equality syllogism, regarding what we have mentioned, falls under the categorical conjunctive, as testified by its definition: that the other statement is mentioned in it by its matter not by its form, and both its premises are categorical. As for what was mentioned that they confined it to the four figures and it does not fall under any of them because they require in them the sharing of the two premises in the middle term, and there is no sharing here, its answer is, as some investigators have pointed out, that they did not require the repetition of the middle term in the sense that without it production would not occur, but rather in the sense that without it knowledge of production would not follow. The upshot: The conditions considered in conjunctive syllogisms are of two types: what is a condition for the occurrence of production, and what is a condition for knowledge of it. The repetition of the middle term is of the second type. And their confinement of the conjunctive syllogism to the four figures is regarding the syllogism that includes the conditions considered for knowledge of production, not absolutely, such that it would entail restricting the universal to some individuals. And it is not hidden what is in it. For we do not concede that knowledge of production does not follow when the middle term is not repeated in the technical sense; rather, when it is not repeated at all, necessarily knowledge of production occurs in the equality syllogism regarding the supposed conclusion, even though the middle term is not repeated in it in the well-known sense among the majority. So reflect. (Mirza Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a lengthy dialectical defense of the status of qiyas al-musawat as a valid categorical syllogism despite lacking the technical repetition of the middle term. The commentator first notes a potential contradiction: earlier it was said qiyas al-musawat essentially produces the intermediate result, so how can it be said not to be from muwasil bi al-dhat? He resolves that the statement applies to the final conclusion, not the intermediate. Then an objection arises: if that is the case, it would restrict the universal to some individuals (i.e., the definition of muwasil would exclude this syllogism). The objector argues that logicians restrict qiyas iqtirani to four figures, and qiyas al-musawat does not fit any because its premises do not share a middle term in the technical sense. Therefore it would be outside the definition of syllogism, yet it is considered a syllogism—contradiction. The commentator responds by distinguishing two types of conditions: those necessary for the actual occurrence of production (intaj) and those necessary for knowledge of production. The repetition of the middle term is only needed for knowledge, not for production itself. Hence, qiyas al-musawat does produce a conclusion (the intermediate), even if we cannot immediately see the final conclusion. The confinement to four figures applies only to syllogisms that satisfy the epistemic conditions. The commentator ends with a critical note: he does not fully accept the distinction, because in qiyas al-musawat knowledge of production does occur without any repetition of the middle term in the sense used by the majority. So the argument remains open.

The Syllogism
intermediate
8 min
The Syllogism of Equality and the Role of the Middle Term
Author argues about classification of qiyas al-musawat and condition of middle term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conditions for production and conditions for knowledge of production in categorical syllogisms, and apply this to evaluate the status of qiyas al-musawat.

Core Idea
The middle term's repetition is epistemologically necessary, not ontologically.

In this passage, the author grapples with a puzzling case: qiyas al-musawat (the syllogism of equality) appears to be a valid syllogism, yet it lacks a shared middle term in the technical sense. How can this be? The key lies in a subtle distinction: some conditions are required for the syllogism to produce a conclusion at all, while others are required for us to know that it produces that conclusion. The repetition of the middle term, the author argues, belongs to the second category. But the commentator, Mirza Muhammad Ali, pushes back: even without repetition, we do know the conclusion in qiyas al-musawat. Let's examine this logical puzzle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem: Qiyas al-musawat defies the four figures
The passage begins by noting that logicians have classified syllogisms exhaustively, yet the syllogism of equality (e.g., A = B, B = C, therefore A = C) does not fit into any of the four figures because it has no repeated middle term. The initial objection is that this would make it an invalid syllogism.
Observe that qiyas al-musawat has three terms but the middle term is not genuinely shared in the same sense as in a standard categorical syllogism.
2
Extract the author's distinction: production vs. knowledge of production
The author responds that the condition of repeating the middle term is not for the syllogism to produce a conclusion (al-intāj), but for us to have knowledge of that production (al-ʿilm bi-l-intāj). Without the repetition, the syllogism still produces its conclusion, but we might not be certain that it does.
This is a key conceptual move: separating ontology from epistemology in logical validity.
3
Test the distinction against qiyas al-musawat
The commentator objects: in qiyas al-musawat, we do have knowledge of the conclusion even without a repeated middle term. For example, if we know A = B and B = C, we immediately know A = C. So the claimed condition for knowledge is not satisfied, and the distinction collapses.
Mirza Muhammad Ali's criticism shows that the epistemic condition is not merely about repetition, but about the form of the argument.
4
Evaluate the implications
This debate reveals that the traditional classification of syllogisms into four figures is based on conditions for epistemic certainty, not for logical validity per se. The case of qiyas al-musawat challenges the completeness of that classification.
The passage ends with 'so reflect', inviting the reader to ponder the tension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في القياس
بيان الملازمة انهم حصروا القياس في الاستثنائى والاقتراني و الاقتراني على الحملى والشرطي و معلوم انه اى القياس المساواة ليس من الاستثنائى ولا الاقتراني الشرطى بقى الاقتراني الحملى وحصروه فى الاشكال الاربعة و ليس بداخل تحت شيء منها للزوم اشتراك المقدمتين في الحد الاوسط بالمعنى الاصطلاحي فيها دونه فثبت انه غير داخل تحت شيء من الاقسام المذكورة للقياس مع انه من افراده كما هو المفروض و هو المطلوب. واما بطلان التالي فظاهر لا يحتاج إلى البيان.
قلت: لا شك فى ان قياس المساواة بالنسبة الى ما ذكرنا داخل تحت الاقتراني الحملى على ما يشهد به تعريفه بانه ما كان القول الاخر فيه مذكوراً بمادته دون هيئته ويكون كلتا مقدمتيه حملية. و اما ما ذكر من انهم حصروه فى الاشكال الاربعة و هو ليس بداخل تحت واحد منها لاشتراطهم فيها اشتراك المقدمتين في الحد الاوسط ولا اشتراك فيه هنا فجوابه على ما أشار اليه بعض المحققين انهم لم يشترطوا تكرر الوسط بمعنى انه لولاه لم يتحقق الانتاج بل بمعنى انه لولاه لم يلزم العلم بالانتاج.
والحاصل: ان الشروط المعتبرة في الاقيسة الاقترانية على نوعين ماهو شرط لتحقق الانتاج وماهو شرط للعلم به و تكرر الوسط من النوع الثاني وحصرهم القياس الاقتراني في الاشكال الاربعة بالنسبة الى القياس المشتمل على الشروط المعتبرة للعلم بالانتاج لا مطلقا حتى يلزم قصر الكلى على بعض الافراد. ولا يخفى ما فيه، فانا لا تسلم انه لا يلزم العلم بالانتاج اذا لم يتكرر الوسط بالمعنى الاصطلاحي بل اذا لم يتكرر مطلقا ضرورة حصول العلم بالانتاج فى قياس المساواة بالنسبة إلى النتيجة المفروضة مع انه لم يتكرر الأوسط فيه بالمعنى المشهور عند الجمهور فتأمل (میرزا محمد علی).
On the syllogism. Explanation of the implication: They restricted the syllogism to the conditional and the conjunctive, and the conjunctive to the categorical and the conditional. It is known that the syllogism of equality is not of the conditional conjunctive nor of the conditional conjunctive? The categorical conjunctive remains, and they restricted it to the four figures. It does not fall under any of them because the two premises must share the middle term in the technical sense in them, but not in it. So it is established that it does not fall under any of the mentioned divisions of the syllogism, even though it is one of its individuals, as is supposed, and that is the desired conclusion. As for the falsehood of the consequent, it is apparent and does not need exposition. I say: There is no doubt that the syllogism of equality, with respect to what we mentioned, falls under the categorical conjunctive, as evidenced by its definition: it is one in which the other statement is mentioned by its matter without its form, and both its premises are categorical. As for what is mentioned that they restricted it to the four figures and it does not fall under any of them because they stipulate in them that the two premises share the middle term, and there is no sharing here, its answer, as indicated by some verifiers, is that they did not stipulate the repetition of the middle term in the sense that without it production would not occur, but rather in the sense that without it knowledge of production would not be necessary. The summary: The conditions considered in conjunctive syllogisms are of two types: what is a condition for the realization of production, and what is a condition for knowledge of it. Repetition of the middle term is of the second type. Their restriction of the conjunctive syllogism to the four figures is with respect to the syllogism that includes the conditions considered for knowledge of production, not absolutely, so that a restriction of the universal to some individuals would follow. And it is not hidden what is in it, for we do not concede that knowledge of production is not necessary when the middle term is not repeated in the technical sense. Rather, when it is not repeated absolutely, knowledge of production necessarily occurs in the syllogism of equality with respect to the assumed conclusion, even though the middle term is not repeated in it in the well-known sense among the majority. So reflect. (Mirza Muhammad Ali)
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a logical discussion about the classification of qiyas al-musawat (syllogism of equality). The author first states the problem: logicians restrict syllogisms to conditional (istithna'i) and conjunctive (iqtirani), and then subdivide conjunctive into categorical (hamli) and conditional (sharti). Qiyas al-musawat does not fall under conditional conjunctive or conditional istithna'i, so it must be under categorical conjunctive. But they also restrict categorical conjunctive to four figures, and qiyas al-musawat does not fit any because it lacks a shared middle term in the technical sense. The apparent conclusion is that qiyas al-musawat is not a valid syllogism. The author responds: The definition of categorical conjunctive does not require a shared middle term; it only requires that the 'other statement' (the conclusion) is mentioned by its matter (subject and predicate) without its form (copula). Qiyas al-musawat satisfies this. As for the four figures, the condition of repetition of the middle term is not for the syllogism to produce a conclusion, but for us to know that it produces a conclusion. The commentator (Mirza Muhammad Ali) then objects: In qiyas al-musawat, we do have knowledge of the conclusion even without repetition of the middle term, so the claimed condition for knowledge is not met. Thus the distinction fails. The passage uses the example of qiyas al-musawat to probe the precise role of the middle term in syllogistic theory. The key point is that the middle term's repetition is epistemologically needed for certainty, not ontologically needed for validity.

Key Terms
الحد الأوسط
الإنتاج
قياس المساواة

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do logicians require the repetition of the middle term in the four figures?
A) Without it, the syllogism cannot produce a conclusion.
B) Without it, the logician cannot have certain knowledge of the conclusion.
C) Without it, the conclusion would be invalid.
D) Without it, the syllogism would not be categorical.

Key Takeaway
The middle term's repetition is epistemologically necessary for certainty, not ontologically for validity, but even this epistemological condition is challenged by qiyas al-musawat.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Consider the argument: 'Every intoxicant is forbidden (haram). Every khamr is an intoxicant. Therefore, every khamr is forbidden.' Identify the middle term. Is its repetition a condition for production or for knowledge? Explain using the distinction from this lesson.
?
Task 2: Construct a qiyas al-musawat example using Islamic legal reasoning. For instance, from the Quran: 'The testimony of two women (A) is equal to the testimony of one man (B).' And 'The testimony of one man (B) is equal to the testimony of one man in a specific ruling? Actually, use a numerical equality from inheritance: 'The share of a wife is 1/8 when children exist (A). The share of a husband is 1/4 when no children exist (B).' That is not equality. Better: 'The blood money for a woman (A) is half the blood money for a man (B). The blood money for a man (B) is the full diya (C). Therefore, the blood money for a woman (A) is half the full diya (C).' This is qiyas al-musawat. Evaluate whether the middle term (blood money for a man) is repeated in the technical sense, and whether knowledge of the conclusion is immediate.
